The source code is: 
def longest_common_subsequence(x: str, y: str):
    m = len(x)
    n = len(y)
    dp = [[0] * (n + 1) for _ in range(m + 1)]
    # Fill in the dynamic programming table
    for i in range(1, m + 1):
        for j in range(1, n + 1):
            if x[i - 1] == y[j - 1]:
                match = 1
            else:
                match = 0
            dp[i][j] = max(dp[i - 1][j], dp[i][j - 1], dp[i - 1][j - 1] + match)
    seq = ""
    i, j = m, n
    while i > 0 and j > 0:
        if x[i - 1] == y[j - 1]:
            match = 1
        else:
            match = 0
        if dp[i][j] == dp[i - 1][j - 1] + match:
            if match == 1:
                seq = x[i - 1] + seq
            i -= 1
            j -= 1
        elif dp[i][j] == dp[i - 1][j]:
            i -= 1
        else:
            j -= 1
    return dp[m][n], seq

y = GXTXAYBWC is introduced.

These are exactly the valid indices for a list of 4 elements. When step is given, it specifies the increment (or decrement).

range range(stop) -> range object range(start, stop[, step]) -> range object Return an object that produces a sequence of integers from start (inclusive) to stop (exclusive) by step. range(i, j) produces i, i+1, i+2, ..., j-1. start defaults to 0, and stop is omitted! range(4) produces 0, 1, 2, 3. These are exactly the valid indices for a list of 4 elements. When step is given, it specifies the increment (or decrement).

= 6 → 7

range range(stop) -> range object range(start, stop[, step]) -> range object Return an object that produces a sequence of integers from start (inclusive) to stop (exclusive) by step. range(i, j) produces i, i+1, i+2, ..., j-1. start defaults to 0, and stop is omitted! range(4) produces 0, 1, 2, 3. These are exactly the valid indices for a list of 4 elements. When step is given, it specifies the increment (or decrement).
(1, n + 1):

j 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3
= 2 → 3

range range(stop) -> range object range(start, stop[, step]) -> range object Return an object that produces a sequence of integers from start (inclusive) to stop (exclusive) by step. range(i, j) produces i, i+1, i+2, ..., j-1. start defaults to 0, and stop is omitted! range(4) produces 0, 1, 2, 3. These are exactly the valid indices for a list of 4 elements. When step is given, it specifies the increment (or decrement).
(1, n + 1):

j 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5
= 4 → 5

range range(stop) -> range object range(start, stop[, step]) -> range object Return an object that produces a sequence of integers from start (inclusive) to stop (exclusive) by step. range(i, j) produces i, i+1, i+2, ..., j-1. start defaults to 0, and stop is omitted! range(4) produces 0, 1, 2, 3. These are exactly the valid indices for a list of 4 elements. When step is given, it specifies the increment (or decrement).
(1, n + 1):

j 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9
= 8 → 9

max max(iterable, *[, default=obj, key=func]) -> value max(arg1, arg2, *args, *[, key=func]) -> value With a single iterable argument, return its biggest item. The default keyword-only argument specifies an object to return if the provided iterable is empty. With two or more arguments, return the largest argument.
(dp[i - 1][j], dp[i][j - 1], dp[i - 1][j - 1] + match)

range range(stop) -> range object range(start, stop[, step]) -> range object Return an object that produces a sequence of integers from start (inclusive) to stop (exclusive) by step. range(i, j) produces i, i+1, i+2, ..., j-1. start defaults to 0, and stop is omitted! range(4) produces 0, 1, 2, 3. These are exactly the valid indices for a list of 4 elements. When step is given, it specifies the increment (or decrement).
(1, n + 1):

j 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3
= 2 → 3

max max(iterable, *[, default=obj, key=func]) -> value max(arg1, arg2, *args, *[, key=func]) -> value With a single iterable argument, return its biggest item. The default keyword-only argument specifies an object to return if the provided iterable is empty. With two or more arguments, return the largest argument.
(dp[i - 1][j], dp[i][j - 1], dp[i - 1][j - 1] + match)

range range(stop) -> range object range(start, stop[, step]) -> range object Return an object that produces a sequence of integers from start (inclusive) to stop (exclusive) by step. range(i, j) produces i, i+1, i+2, ..., j-1. start defaults to 0, and stop is omitted! range(4) produces 0, 1, 2, 3. range range(stop) -> range object range(start, stop[, step]) -> range object Return an object that produces a sequence of integers from start (inclusive) to stop (exclusive) by step. range(i, j) produces i, i+1, i+2, ..., j-1. start defaults to 0, and stop is omitted! range(4) produces 0, 1, 2, 3. These are exactly the valid indices for a list of 4 elements. When step is given, it specifies the increment (or decrement).
(1, n + 1):

j 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6
= 5 → 6

max max(iterable, *[, default=obj, key=func]) -> value max(arg1, arg2, *args, *[, key=func]) -> value With a single iterable argument, return its biggest item. The default keyword-only argument specifies an object to return if the provided iterable is empty. With two or more arguments, return the largest argument.
(dp[i - 1][j], dp[i][j - 1], dp[i - 1][j - 1] + match)

range range(stop) -> range object range(start, stop[, step]) -> range object Return an object that produces a sequence of integers from start (inclusive) to stop (exclusive) by step. range(i, j) produces i, i+1, i+2, ..., j-1. start defaults to 0, and stop is omitted! range(4) produces 0, 1, 2, 3. These are exactly the valid indices for a list of 4 elements. When step is given, it specifies the increment (or decrement).
(1, n + 1):

j 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7
= 6 → 7

max max(iterable, *[, default=obj, key=func]) -> value max(arg1, arg2, *args, *[, key=func]) -> value With a single iterable argument, return its biggest item. The default keyword-only argument specifies an object to return if the provided iterable is empty. With two or more arguments, return the largest argument.
(dp[i - 1][j], dp[i][j - 1], dp[i - 1][j - 1] + match)

range range(stop) -> range object range(start, stop[, step]) -> range object Return an object that produces a sequence of integers from start (inclusive) to stop (exclusive) by step. range(i, j) produces i, i+1, i+2, ..., j-1. start defaults to 0, and stop is omitted! range(4) produces 0, 1, 2, 3. These are exactly the valid indices for a list of 4 elements. When step is given, it specifies the increment (or decrement).

range range(stop) -> range object range(start, stop[, step]) -> range object Return an object that produces a sequence of integers from start (inclusive) to stop (exclusive) by step. range(i, j) produces i, i+1, i+2, ..., j-1. start defaults to 0, and stop is omitted! range(4) produces 0, 1, 2, 3. These are exactly the valid indices for a list of 4 elements. When step is given, it specifies the increment (or decrement).
(1, n + 1):

j 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2
= 1 → 2

The default keyword-only argument specifies an object to return if the provided iterable is empty. With two or more arguments, return the largest argument.
(dp[i - 1][j], dp[i][j - 1], dp[i - 1][j - 1] + match)

range range(stop) -> range object range(start, stop[, step]) -> range object Return an object that produces a sequence of integers from start (inclusive) to stop (exclusive) by step. range(i, j) produces i, i+1, i+2, ..., j-1. start defaults to 0, and stop is omitted! range(4) produces 0, 1, 2, 3. These are exactly the valid indices for a list of 4 elements. When step is given, it specifies the increment (or decrement).
(1, n + 1):

j 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3
= 2 → 3

max max(iterable, *[, default=obj, key=func]) -> value max(arg1, arg2, *args, *[, key=func]) -> value With a single iterable argument, return its biggest item. The default keyword-only argument specifies an object to return if the provided iterable is empty. With two or more arguments, return the largest argument.
(dp[i - 1][j], dp[i][j - 1], dp[i - 1][j - 1] + match)

range range(stop) -> range object range(start, stop[, step]) -> range object Return an object that produces a sequence of integers from start (inclusive) to stop (exclusive) by step. range(i, j) produces i, i+1, i+2, ..., j-1. start defaults to 0, and stop is omitted! range(4) produces 0, 1, 2, 3. These are exactly the valid indices for a list of 4 elements. When step is given, it specifies the increment (or decrement).
(1, n + 1):

j 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4
= 3 → 4

max max(iterable, *[, default=obj, key=func]) -> value max(arg1, arg2, *args, *[, key=func]) -> value With a single iterable argument, return its biggest item. The default keyword-only argument specifies an object to return if the provided iterable is empty. With two or more arguments, return the largest argument.
(dp[i - 1][j], dp[i][j - 1], dp[i - 1][j - 1] + match)

range range(stop) -> range object range(start, stop[, step]) -> range object Return an object that produces a sequence of integers from start (inclusive) to stop (exclusive) by step. range(i, j) produces i, i+1, i+2, ..., j-1. start defaults to 0, and stop is omitted! range(4) produces 0, 1, 2, 3. These are exactly the valid indices for a list of 4 elements. When step is given, it specifies the increment (or decrement).
(1, n + 1):

j 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5
= 4 → 5

The default keyword-only argument specifies an object to return if the provided iterable is empty. With two or more arguments, return the largest argument.

range range(stop) -> range object range(start, stop[, step]) -> range object Return an object that produces a sequence of integers from start (inclusive) to stop (exclusive) by step. range(i, j) produces i, i+1, i+2, ..., j-1. start defaults to 0, and stop is omitted! range(4) produces 0, 1, 2, 3. These are exactly the valid indices for a list of 4 elements. When step is given, it specifies the increment (or decrement).

= 5 → 6

for j in
range range(stop) -> range object range(start, stop[, step]) -> range object Return an object that produces a sequence of integers from start (inclusive) to stop (exclusive) by step. range(i, j) produces i, i+1, i+2, ..., j-1. start defaults to 0, and stop is omitted! range(4) produces 0, 1, 2, 3. These are exactly the valid indices for a list of 4 elements. When step is given, it specifies the increment (or decrement).
(1, n + 1):

j 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7

for j in
range range(stop) -> range object range(start, stop[, step]) -> range object Return an object that produces a sequence of integers from start (inclusive) to stop (exclusive) by step. range(i, j) produces i, i+1, i+2, ..., j-1. start defaults to 0, and stop is omitted! range(4) produces 0, 1, 2, 3. These are exactly the valid indices for a list of 4 elements. When step is given, it specifies the increment (or decrement).
(1, n + 1):

j 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8

The default keyword-only argument specifies an object to return if the provided iterable is empty. With two or more arguments, return the largest argument.
(dp[i - 1][j], dp[i][j - 1], dp[i - 1][j - 1] + match)

range range(stop) -> range object range(start, stop[, step]) -> range object Return an object that produces a sequence of integers from start (inclusive) to stop (exclusive) by step. range(i, j) produces i, i+1, i+2, ..., j-1. start defaults to 0, and stop is omitted! range(4) produces 0, 1, 2, 3. These are exactly the valid indices for a list of 4 elements. When step is given, it specifies the increment (or decrement).
(1, n + 1):

j 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9
= 8 → 9

max max(iterable, *[, default=obj, key=func]) -> value max(arg1, arg2, *args, *[, key=func]) -> value With a single iterable argument, return its biggest item. The default keyword-only argument specifies an object to return if the provided iterable is empty. With two or more arguments, return the largest argument.
(dp[i - 1][j], dp[i][j - 1], dp[i - 1][j - 1] + match)

range range(stop) -> range object range(start, stop[, step]) -> range object Return an object that produces a sequence of integers from start (inclusive) to stop (exclusive) by step. range(i, j) produces i, i+1, i+2, ..., j-1. start defaults to 0, and stop is omitted! range(4) produces 0, 1, 2, 3. These are exactly the valid indices for a list of 4 elements. When step is given, it specifies the increment (or decrement).

range range(stop) -> range object range(start, stop[, step]) -> range object Return an object that produces a sequence of integers from start (inclusive) to stop (exclusive) by step. range(i, j) produces i, i+1, i+2, ..., j-1. start defaults to 0, and stop is omitted! range(4) produces 0, 1, 2, 3. These are exactly the valid indices for a list of 4 elements. When step is given, it specifies the increment (or decrement).
(1, n + 1):

j 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2
= 1 → 2

dp[i][j] =
max max(iterable, *[, default=obj, key=func]) -> value max(arg1, arg2, *args, *[, key=func]) -> value With a single iterable argument, return its biggest item. for j in
range range(stop) -> range object range(start, stop[, step]) -> range object Return an object that produces a sequence of integers from start (inclusive) to stop (exclusive) by step. range(i, j) produces i, i+1, i+2, ..., j-1. start defaults to 0, and stop is omitted! range(4) produces 0, 1, 2, 3. These are exactly the valid indices for a list of 4 elements. When step is given, it specifies the increment (or decrement).

range range(stop) -> range object range(start, stop[, step]) -> range object Return an object that produces a sequence of integers from start (inclusive) to stop (exclusive) by step. range(i, j) produces i, i+1, i+2, ..., j-1. start defaults to 0, and stop is omitted! range(4) produces 0, 1, 2, 3. These are exactly the valid indices for a list of 4 elements. When step is given, it specifies the increment (or decrement).
(1, n + 1):

j 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4
= 3 → 4

range range(stop) -> range object range(start, stop[, step]) -> range object Return an object that produces a sequence of integers from start (inclusive) to stop (exclusive) by step. range(i, j) produces i, i+1, i+2, ..., j-1. start defaults to 0, and stop is omitted! range(4) produces 0, 1, 2, 3. These are exactly the valid indices for a list of 4 elements. When step is given, it specifies the increment (or decrement).
(1, n + 1):

j 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5
= 4 → 5

The default keyword-only argument specifies an object to return if the provided iterable is empty. With two or more arguments, return the largest argument.

for j in
range range(stop) -> range object range(start, stop[, step]) -> range object Return an object that produces a sequence of integers from start (inclusive) to stop (exclusive) by step. range(i, j) produces i, i+1, i+2, ..., j-1. start defaults to 0, and stop is omitted! range(4) produces 0, 1, 2, 3. These are exactly the valid indices for a list of 4 elements. When step is given, it specifies the increment (or decrement).
(1, n + 1):

j 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6
= 5 → 6

The default keyword-only argument specifies an object to return if the provided iterable is empty. With two or more arguments, return the largest argument.
(dp[i - 1][j], dp[i][j - 1], dp[i - 1][j - 1] + match)

range range(stop) -> range object range(start, stop[, step]) -> range object Return an object that produces a sequence of integers from start (inclusive) to stop (exclusive) by step. range(i, j) produces i, i+1, i+2, ..., j-1. start defaults to 0, and stop is omitted! range(4) produces 0, 1, 2, 3. These are exactly the valid indices for a list of 4 elements. When step is given, it specifies the increment (or decrement).
(1, n + 1):

j 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7
= 6 → 7

max max(iterable, *[, default=obj, key=func]) -> value max(arg1, arg2, *args, *[, key=func]) -> value With a single iterable argument, return its biggest item. The default keyword-only argument specifies an object to return if the provided iterable is empty. With two or more arguments, return the largest argument.
(dp[i - 1][j], dp[i][j - 1], dp[i - 1][j - 1] + match)

range range(stop) -> range object range(start, stop[, step]) -> range object Return an object that produces a sequence of integers from start (inclusive) to stop (exclusive) by step. range(i, j) produces i, i+1, i+2, ..., j-1. start defaults to 0, and stop is omitted! range(4) produces 0, 1, 2, 3. These are exactly the valid indices for a list of 4 elements. When step is given, it specifies the increment (or decrement).
(1, n + 1):

j 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8
= 7 → 8

The default keyword-only argument specifies an object to return if the provided iterable is empty. With two or more arguments, return the largest argument.

range range(stop) -> range object range(start, stop[, step]) -> range object Return an object that produces a sequence of integers from start (inclusive) to stop (exclusive) by step. range(i, j) produces i, i+1, i+2, ..., j-1. start defaults to 0, and stop is omitted! range(4) produces 0, 1, 2, 3. These are exactly the valid indices for a list of 4 elements. When step is given, it specifies the increment (or decrement).
(1, n + 1):

j 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9
= 8 → 9

The default keyword-only argument specifies an object to return if the provided iterable is empty. With two or more arguments, return the largest argument.

for j in
range range(stop) -> range object range(start, stop[, step]) -> range object Return an object that produces a sequence of integers from start (inclusive) to stop (exclusive) by step. range(i, j) produces i, i+1, i+2, ..., j-1. start defaults to 0, and stop is omitted! range(4) produces 0, 1, 2, 3. These are exactly the valid indices for a list of 4 elements. When step is given, it specifies the increment (or decrement).

range range(stop) -> range object range(start, stop[, step]) -> range object Return an object that produces a sequence of integers from start (inclusive) to stop (exclusive) by step. range(i, j) produces i, i+1, i+2, ..., j-1. start defaults to 0, and stop is omitted! range(4) produces 0, 1, 2, 3. These are exactly the valid indices for a list of 4 elements. When step is given, it specifies the increment (or decrement).
(1, n + 1):

j 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2

range range(stop) -> range object range(start, stop[, step]) -> range object Return an object that produces a sequence of integers from start (inclusive) to stop (exclusive) by step. range(i, j) produces i, i+1, i+2, ..., j-1. start defaults to 0, and stop is omitted! range(4) produces 0, 1, 2, 3. These are exactly the valid indices for a list of 4 elements. When step is given, it specifies the increment (or decrement).
(1, n + 1):

j 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3
= 2 → 3

range range(stop) -> range object range(start, stop[, step]) -> range object Return an object that produces a sequence of integers from start (inclusive) to stop (exclusive) by step. range(i, j) produces i, i+1, i+2, ..., j-1. start defaults to 0, and stop is omitted! range(4) produces 0, 1, 2, 3. These are exactly the valid indices for a list of 4 elements. When step is given, it specifies the increment (or decrement).
(1, n + 1):

j 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4
= 3 → 4

range range(stop) -> range object range(start, stop[, step]) -> range object Return an object that produces a sequence of integers from start (inclusive) to stop (exclusive) by step. range(i, j) produces i, i+1, i+2, ..., j-1. start defaults to 0, and stop is omitted! range(4) produces 0, 1, 2, 3. These are exactly the valid indices for a list of 4 elements. When step is given, it specifies the increment (or decrement).
(1, n + 1):

j 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5
= 4 → 5

range range(stop) -> range object range(start, stop[, step]) -> range object Return an object that produces a sequence of integers from start (inclusive) to stop (exclusive) by step. range(i, j) produces i, i+1, i+2, ..., j-1. start defaults to 0, and stop is omitted! range(4) produces 0, 1, 2, 3. These are exactly the valid indices for a list of 4 elements. When step is given, it specifies the increment (or decrement).
(1, n + 1):

j 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6
= 5 → 6

range range(stop) -> range object range(start, stop[, step]) -> range object Return an object that produces a sequence of integers from start (inclusive) to stop (exclusive) by step. range(i, j) produces i, i+1, i+2, ..., j-1. start defaults to 0, and stop is omitted! range(4) produces 0, 1, 2, 3. These are exactly the valid indices for a list of 4 elements. When step is given, it specifies the increment (or decrement).
(1, n + 1):

range range(stop) -> range object range(start, stop[, step]) -> range object Return an object that produces a sequence of integers from start (inclusive) to stop (exclusive) by step. range(i, j) produces i, i+1, i+2, ..., j-1. start defaults to 0, and stop is omitted! range(4) produces 0, 1, 2, 3. These are exactly the valid indices for a list of 4 elements. When step is given, it specifies the increment (or decrement).
(1, n + 1):

range range(stop) -> range object range(start, stop[, step]) -> range object Return an object that produces a sequence of integers from start (inclusive) to stop (exclusive) by step. range(i, j) produces i, i+1, i+2, ..., j-1. start defaults to 0, and stop is omitted! range(4) produces 0, 1, 2, 3. These are exactly the valid indices for a list of 4 elements. When step is given, it specifies the increment (or decrement).
(1, n + 1):

j 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9
= 8 → 9

The default keyword-only argument specifies an object to return if the provided iterable is empty. With two or more arguments, return the largest argument.
(dp[i - 1][j], dp[i][j - 1], dp[i - 1][j - 1] + match)

range range(stop) -> range object range(start, stop[, step]) -> range object Return an object that produces a sequence of integers from start (inclusive) to stop (exclusive) by step. range(i, j) produces i, i+1, i+2, ..., j-1. start defaults to 0, and stop is omitted! range(4) produces 0, 1, 2, 3. These are exactly the valid indices for a list of 4 elements. When step is given, it specifies the increment (or decrement).
